# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Perfect! I've completed the comprehensive audit of Envoy's access log format field implementations. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all C++ source files that implement access log command operators in envoyproxy/envoy v1.31.2. The implementation consists of:

### Key Files (8 total):
1. **substitution_formatter.h/cc** - Main parser that tokenizes format strings
2. **http_specific_formatter.h/cc** - HTTP-specific operators (%REQ%, %RESP%, %TRAILER%, etc.)
3. **stream_info_formatter.h/cc** - Stream info operators (%DURATION%, %UPSTREAM_HOST%, etc.)
4. **substitution_format_utility.h/cc** - Utility functions

### Command Operators Found:

**HTTP-Specific (via HttpBuiltInCommandParser):**
- %REQ(header)% - Request headers
- %RESP(header)% - Response headers  
- %TRAILER(header)% - Response trailers
- %GRPC_STATUS%, %TRACE_ID%, %LOCAL_REPLY_BODY%, etc.

**Stream Info (via getKnownStreamInfoFormatterProviders):**
- **%DURATION%** - Current request duration (line 1034-1041)
- **%UPSTREAM_HOST%** - Upstream host with port (line 1084-1100)
- Plus 100+ other operators for:
  - Bytes metrics (BYTES_RECEIVED, BYTES_SENT, etc.)
  - Durations (REQUEST_DURATION, RESPONSE_DURATION, etc.)
  - Addresses (all variants of upstream/downstream addresses)
  - SSL/TLS information
  - Metadata and filter state
  - Timing information

### Implementation Pattern:
Commands are resolved through a chain:
1. SubstitutionFormatParser.parse() → tokenizes
2. HttpBuiltInCommandParser.parse() → handles HTTP commands
3. StreamInfoFormatterBase → handles stream info commands via getKnownStreamInfoFormatterProviders()

Overview\\n\\nThe Envoy access log formatting system is implemented across multiple source files in the `source/common/formatter/` directory. The system uses a two-level command parsing approach:\\n\\n1. **HTTP-specific commands** registered in `HttpBuiltInCommandParser` (source/common/formatter/http_specific_formatter.cc)\\n2. **Stream info commands** registered in `getKnownStreamInfoFormatterProviders()` (source/common/formatter/stream_info_formatter.cc)\\n\\n## Command Operator Implementation\\n\\n### HTTP-Specific Operators (%REQ%, %RESP%, etc.)\\n\\nThese are implemented in `source/common/formatter/http_specific_formatter.cc` via the `HttpBuiltInCommandParser::getKnownFormatters()` function, which registers the following command operators:\\n\\n- **%REQ(header-name)%** - Implemented via `RequestHeaderFormatter` class. Formats request headers with optional max length truncation.\\n- **%RESP(header-name)%** - Implemented via `ResponseHeaderFormatter` class. Formats response headers.\\n- **%TRAILER(header-name)%** - Implemented via `ResponseTrailerFormatter` class. Formats response trailers.\\n- **%LOCAL_REPLY_BODY%** - Implemented via `LocalReplyBodyFormatter` class.\\n- **%ACCESS_LOG_TYPE%** - Implemented via `AccessLogTypeFormatter` class.\\n- **%GRPC_STATUS%** - Implemented via `GrpcStatusFormatter` class. Supports CAMEL_STRING, SNAKE_STRING, and NUMBER formats.\\n- **%GRPC_STATUS_NUMBER%** - Shorthand for GRPC_STATUS with NUMBER format.\\n- **%REQUEST_HEADERS_BYTES%** - Implemented via `HeadersByteSizeFormatter`.\\n- **%RESPONSE_HEADERS_BYTES%** - Implemented via `HeadersByteSizeFormatter`.\\n- **%RESPONSE_TRAILERS_BYTES%** - Implemented via `HeadersByteSizeFormatter`.\\n- **%STREAM_INFO_REQ(header-name)%** - Alternative request header formatter using stream info.\\n- **%TRACE_ID%** - Implemented via `TraceIDFormatter` class.\\n\\n### Stream Info Operators (%DURATION%, %UPSTREAM_HOST%, etc.)\\n\\nThese are implemented in `source/common/formatter/stream_info_formatter.cc` via the `getKnownStreamInfoFormatterProviders()` function, which returns a `StreamInfoFormatterProviderLookupTable` (flat_hash_map) containing:\\n\\n#### Duration-Related Operators:\\n- **%REQUEST_DURATION%** - Time from first downstream RX byte to last downstream RX byte\\n- **%REQUEST_TX_DURATION%** - Time from first to last upstream TX byte\\n- **%RESPONSE_DURATION%** - Time from first upstream RX byte\\n- **%RESPONSE_TX_DURATION%** - Duration between downstream and upstream response\\n- **%DOWNSTREAM_HANDSHAKE_DURATION%** - Downstream connection handshake duration\\n- **%ROUNDTRIP_DURATION%** - Complete roundtrip duration\\n- **%DURATION%** - Current request duration from stream info (line 1034-1041)\\n- **%COMMON_DURATION(...)%** - Configurable duration between arbitrary time points (line 1042-1046)\\n- **%UPSTREAM_CONNECTION_POOL_READY_DURATION%** - Connection pool callback latency (line 1737-1756)\\n\\n#### Bytes-Related Operators:\\n- **%BYTES_RECEIVED%** - Downstream bytes received\\n- **%BYTES_SENT%** - Downstream bytes sent\\n- **%BYTES_RETRANSMITTED%** - TCP retransmitted bytes\\n- **%PACKETS_RETRANSMITTED%** - TCP retransmitted packets\\n- **%UPSTREAM_WIRE_BYTES_RECEIVED%** - Upstream wire bytes received\\n- **%UPSTREAM_HEADER_BYTES_RECEIVED%** - Upstream header bytes received\\n- **%UPSTREAM_WIRE_BYTES_SENT%** - Upstream wire bytes sent\\n- **%UPSTREAM_HEADER_BYTES_SENT%** - Upstream header bytes sent\\n- **%DOWNSTREAM_WIRE_BYTES_RECEIVED%** - Downstream wire bytes received\\n- **%DOWNSTREAM_HEADER_BYTES_RECEIVED%** -
